  1. I saw this infomercial on TV and I didn't want to get sucked into being charged automatically for a new shipment every 3 months. So I ordered it from here so I could try it. My hair was color-treated and very damaged. My hair is also very thick and curly. I tried this the first day I got it and was amazed. Now only two uses later, I am having trouble finding my split ends that used to overpower my hair!!! It is a great product. My hair is sooo soft now and manageable, it also smells wonderful. You need to be careful not to use it as a leave-in if you are prone to greasy hair, but the product itself, when rinsed out did not leave a greasy feeling in my hair. I will definitely continue to buy this product. Unlike claims that you should not always shampoo your hair and just condition it that leave it feeling unclean, this product left my hair feeling very clean and feeling amazing.

  3. Okay, let me start off by saying that my hair extremely dry, brittle and weak. From years of relaxing and over-processing it with color treatments and relaxers, my hair had grown rough and unmanageable. Even when I would wash it with \\"good\\" shampoo and conditioner my hair would feel very rough after rinse out. Especially considering I had colored my hair black about a week earlier. After my first time using Wen, I noticed a BIG difference, it was great! My hair was straighter, less frizzy, a little more volume and it actually moved *shock*! It also had this radiant shine that I don't think I've EVER seen before which is a huge plus. With each wash, I'm noticing that my hair is getting better with time.I did exactly what the instructions said, except I use a shower/plastic cap after application (30+ pumps) and leave it on for at least 10 minutes or more. After I rinse it out completely, I'll add a few more pumps to my hair then massage and re-rinse (kind of like a rinse out conditioner). From there, I blow dry then curl with a Conair instant heat curling iron and apply oil sheen. I then brush and wrap my hair (and if it's night time I'll apply a silk scarf). I don't use Wen as a leave in conditioner anymore because it might be a little much for my hair. If your hair gets easily \\"over-moist\\" or oily, you may want to switch shampoos between using Wen every now and then. After my third wash, my hair is AMAZING. It's so shiny, vibrant and silky that I'm thinking of getting a years supply. Considering what the conditioner has done, I can't wait to see how the Wen Hydrating Mask does. If you are thinking about using it, try it! Even if you get the smallest size available see what this great conditioner can do for you and you hair.

This entails wetting your hair, applying TONS and TONS of the product to your hair (if you only use a little, your hair will feel dirty and sticky), then wetting your hair again and combing the product through, THEN you have to rinse your hair for a very long time to make sure all the product is out. For these reasons, I would not buy the product again. Not so much because of the time it takes to use, but more because of the amount of product you must use. It's just not cost effective. You can buy a high quality shampoo/conditioner for more money....and it will actually be more cost effective because you will use alot less of the product. I got my Wen about a week and a half ago and I am almost out. Summary: CONS = takes a lot of time to use. You must use a TON of the product. Website locks you into a long term contract. PROS= Does not \\"strip\\" your hair like a regular shampoo. Works as well as a high quality salon shampoo/conditioner.

I use more of the Lavendar when I feel I want more body to my hair, and I also add Wen Tea Tree cleansing conditioner when my scalp is dry/flaky etc. If you have never tried Wen products, I would recommend trying Wen Sweet Almond Mint first as it is the most universal for all hair types and then you can always add another type of Wen cleansing conditioner as you want to. I would also recommend keep a watch out on QVC for demonstrations by the developer of Wen products. He is excellent in demonstrating and teaching exactly how to use and get the most out of this product. I want to say one more thing regarding how much this product saves me money. Before using only Wen products on my hair, I was having to have my hair colored about every two to three months and now that I use only Wen products with the exception of occasional hairspray in the front, I just went 7 months between coloring. I only had the grey hair showing thru in the front and top of my hair where I use the hairspray. So be careful when you see something that claims to work for EVERYTHING. 2) Also, he mentioned that aside from product quality or not, it had genius marketing. Think about it... Wen doesnt really tell you what it DOES do, it tells you what it DOESNT do (lather). So... that is an immediate attention-getter for any consumer. People rush to gobble this stuff up, almost as a marketing brainwash. All of our lives we have heard advertisments describe the benefits of things.... how great it will be, all the wonders the product will do, etc. So we tune things out because it turns into a redundant schpeal (sp?). BUT.... now we have something that tells us what it WONT do, and that any product that DOES do this is harmful. Now you have our attention again. And do your research without buying into new information.... is it really TRUE that lathering is bad? Or are we buying it because in no way, shape, or form could this infomercial be misguiding us...? 3) And using 8 pumps of Wen PER SECTION??? And every day?? Another huge genius marketing campaign... In other words... use your product up as fast as you can so you can run back and buy more. Careful people.... That being said, I have been using Wen off and on for a while now and this is my advice.... 1) Wen claims its safe for every day use. I believe in moderation. Dont use ANY kind of product EVERY single day. Your hair will eventuallyget used to it, get bored with it, and start drying out, and once again youll be back on the market looking for the next miracle product. Plus, like I mentioned above, its part of their marketing campaign. So, what I recommend doing is if youre going to use Wen, combine it with other products... shampoo if you still want to use it, other cleansing conditioners, whatever. Keep everything in moderation. 2 And just use however many pumps feels good to you. I do not divide my hair and use 8 pumps per section. Heck no! Thats just ASKING for greasy hair as well! Waaaay too much product exposure. I have shoulder-length moderately thick hair, and even I just use three pumps for my whole head. I comb it in, leave it in, and go about my shower, then rinse it out at the very end. 3) I also use shampoo in addition to using Wen. This is just personal preference and I prefer the feeling of the clean hair from shampoo before applying the conditioner. 4) Something I dont like about Wen is that my hair seems to be going limp on day 2. I dont wash my hair everyday (more like every 2-3). My hair doesnt get oily easy at all, but on day 2 it seems to be losing its life, its bounce. Its flat to my head, unlike previous years where \\"Day 2 hair\\" was always my favorite. I like how right after using Wen and blow-drying it, I barely have to straighten my hair with a hot iron anymore. Wen has taken out a lot of that frizz and thats whats kept me coming back. However, it seems to have taken its course, because now, its fine and limp all the time... and doesnt Wen say its the BEST for limp hair?? Now this is what is bothering me.... I went in to my hairstylist yesterday for a cut, and he mentioned he has noticed lots of changes in my hair over the past 6 months (since starting Wen). And I didnt mention a thing about Wen either, that was left out of the conversation. He mentioned my hair is not as bouncy anymore, that it appeared a lot more limp... So even HE was noticing it! :( Without knowing about Wen, he said my hair seemed to be *way over conditioned.* My antenna immediately went up. Over-conditioned... hmmmm... sounds familiar.... And what product has been tattooed to our brains that we need to use everyday.....? Wen Cleansing Conditioner... He said conditioning after shampoo (depending on how often you wash your hair) should never be an every-time ordeal. This will dry out your hair and lead to limp, lifeless hair eventually. Funny he would mention.... Am I saying dont use Wen? No. Am I gonna continue to use it? Probably. But Im definitly going to use it even less moderately now, and make sure I incorporate other products for the overall health of my hair. Il probably eventually phase it out completely. I want my bounce back! My advice to you is to just do what works for you. Find out what your Wen-routine turns into, should you decide to keep using it. And dont be afraid to start out with the beginners kit and cancel from there, its really not that tedious. But let them know you dont want anything in the mail or via email asking you to come back either, cause they get you that way too. :) Watch out for marketing red flags, and know that even if something sounds miraculous, everything works differently on different people. Blessings everyone!

So here's a thing, for those who are new to sulfate free shampoo, the whole idea is not use detergent to clean your hair like most regular shampoo so if you use a lot of styling products like gel, hairspray, moose, or those silicon base serum that result in lots of buildup, this WILL NOT effectively clean your hair. I don't use styling products so I love sulfate free products, gently clean without stripping hair of natural beneficial oil. But even as a sulfate free shampoo, for those of you who are like me with oily scalps, this WILL NOT give you that clean feeling if you want to skip washing your hair everyday. I tried it as intended for about two weeks and I really can't stand it, as much as I love my hair after I shower, I always feel gross and dirty at the end of the day. The hair care process is a bit more time-consuming than I hoped for. You wet hair THOROUGHLY (1-2 minutes), lather 16-32+ pumps into hair (3-4 minutes), comb through (1 minute), leave it in for duration of shower (however long that means for you -- keep lathering throughout shower), rinse (1-2 minutes -- it's a lot of product to rinse out), apply leave-in conditioner and styling creme. You have to really focus on what you're doing with the Wen in you hair, so not only does that take more effort than regular shampooing and conditioner, but more time in the shower (which, for water conservers may be a big downside). The product is also thick enough to clog a weak drain, so be careful. My last downside is that the 30-day or 90-day packages do not last that long. Following Chaz's instructions of using about 40 pumps every time I shower, my regimen lasted no more than 16 days. My advice is to use as LITTLE of it at a time as possible. He recommends the more the merrier; I say, use a moderate amount (at most 12 pumps for REALLY THICK hair in the shower) and cleanse more frequently than before. Now for the results: it's pretty good. [[ASIN:B003PXZI2O WEN BY CHAZ DEAN SWEET ALMOND CONDITIONER,STYLING CREME, RE-MOIST MASK INTENSIVE HAIR TREATMENT,TEXTURE BALM,WIDE TOOTH SHOWER COMB,5 PIECE SET]] As a fellow insomniac, I thought I would try the starter pack as shown on the infomercial (NOTE: If you buy the starter kit from the TV, you get another product, the volumizer). My hair is baby-fine, but damaged from coloring. Here's my experience with the Wen products: As stated by others, you DON'T need to use all the pumps as recommended--you'll find how many pumps you need to coat your hair (let the pumping mechanism come all the way to the top between pumps--Wen shampoo/conditioner is thick). The comb that you get as a free gift is EXTREMELY useful for getting the product all over your hair; I was surprised at how much of a difference it made (the same goes for rinsing it out, as well). Leave it in until you are ready to get out of the shower. It takes a while to rinse out, so make sure you have enough hot/warm water available. The first time I used the Wen shampoo, I did it according to the directions, and I had the greasiest, limpest, most scraggly hair a person could have--I looked as though I hadn't washed my hair in a year. The second time I used it, I only used enough to coat my thin hair (about 3 pumps, total) and only left it in for about four minutes. I was extremely pleased with the results when I used it as it seemed to make sense to ME. Like every product on the market, the seller wants you to buy more, so they give you directions to put a whole lot in your hair. Use common sense, and the bottle will last a lot longer. When my current bottle runs out, I may try the type for oily/baby fine hair (I think it's the cucumber extract shampoo). I work at home and don't do much to get dirty, so I only need to wash my hair about once a week; everything I got in the $29.99 kit should last me quite a long time. When it comes to the other four products in the starter kit, I gave the deep conditioner away, since I use warm EVOO (extra virgin olive oil) as a deep hair conditioner. The Wen literature even suggests that people with fine hair should take it easy with the deep conditioner, so at least they are honest about it. My next door neighbor has beautiful thick hair, and she LOVED the deep conditioner! I REALLY like the Styling Creme. When I first looked at it, I thought it would make my hair goopy and droopy, but it didn't--it's an excellent styling product that keeps split ends and flyaway hairs under control, and it does NOT make your hair greasy. I'm now confident enough to use a gracious plenty when I put it on my hair. It's like a creme mousse, and it does the job. You can put it anywhere in your hair where you need some help keeping your hair in one shape--it's not just for the bottom half of your total hair length, which is what the directions tell you to do. I have a portion of my hair that is a cowlick and grows in a funky shape, no matter how long the shaft of the hair is. The Texture Balm works wonders to straighten my damaged/genetically bad clump of hair when I put it on the bottom half of the shaft. Any more than that, and it makes my hair look greasy. Use this product with restraint. However, once you figure out what amount and the placement of it that works for YOUR head, it's a godsend. The Volumizer is basically hair spray, but you only need a little. I really like it, mainly because it doesn't make your hair too stiff and because it doesn't have the heavy, perfume-y smell that most hair sprays have. These four products are all I need (along with a hair dryer and a good brush) to keep my hair looking nice. I seem to get better results if I rinse the cleanser/conditioner with cool water instead of the hot water I enjoy on my skin. Also, I use the \\"low\\" setting on my hair dryer (and just use forced air at the end of my styling--my hair dryer has a button that takes away all the heat, and just blows room temperature air), and I make sureI don't use metal and heat together as I dry my hair--I pick one, depending on where I am in the process of drying/styling my hair. I'm very sensitive to perfumes, and was quite wary of ordering ANY product that isn't unscented, but I found that I didn't have any asthma attacks, or even notice the smell after I rinsed it out or used the hairdryer. Now, when I use my old shampoo, my hair seems frizzy and dry. I truly like the results I get with Wen, it's nice to have some hairspray and a styling creme that doesn't bombard my lungs (I've had to go without either one for over 15 years because of asthma and perfumes). It's quite nice that the whole line has the same scent. I often wonder why women waste money on perfume when their shampoo, conditioner, mousse, hair spray, laundry detergent, fabric softener and skin lotions are all scented, and each one has a different scent to boot! At least several of the above-mentioned products will smell the same, although there will still be a mixture of other perfumes from other products UNLESS you buy scent-free everything (it's not that hard to do--stores are carrying unscented versions of their laundry products and a store called NEEDS--go to [...] an unscented version of everything you can think of that you would put on your body, in your laundry, or use to clean your home. Give your nose a rest, and check out their VAST array of unscented products. The only thing I don't like about the line is the price, but if you look hard enough, bargains can be had. Wen will never be as inexpensive as Suave, but you get what you pay for. Incidentally, you don't have to have a monthly delivery of all of the products. Wen will customize a delivery system for you, even if it's only one product every six months. If you want some time to try it out, get the starter kit, unsubscribe yourself from the monthly delivery, and see how much and how quickly you use of certain products. I think this is the only thing I have ever boughtfrom an infomercial that I truly think was worth the money (wait--Bare Escentuals mineral cosmetics is fantastic, too--I bought it when it was first advertised, and I absolutely love it.).

I use a penny size amount all over my hair, working from tip to root. This product is doesnt weigh hair down or make it greasy. This product helps maintain smooth, styled hair. I use it before blowdrying for a salon finished look.<br /><br />Volumizing Spray: I love this in the lavendar because it is like aromatherapy. This product is one of the best I ever used. I learned it is a 2 in one product. The purpose is to spray roots as you blow dry damp hair for added volume and lift. I have used dozens of mouses, gels & spritzes and have never seen lift like this. You can get as much or as little volume as you want, and it lasts! It doesnt feel like you have any product in your hair. There is nothing worse than having that stiff, heavy feel at the roots. Now, I also discovered a 2nd use for this product!! It makes a great setting spray to use with rollers and curling irons. It sets hair without it being sticky. Best of all, if you need a change, it brushes out leaving hair as soft as when you washed it. I used it to set my hair for a curly updo and then decided to brush it out and set it in rollers for a hair down wavy look. If I had used hairspray my hair would have been dry, sticky, and oil at the scalp. I burshed my hair out and it felt \\"just washed\\" and soft. I was able to respray and reset my hair and the wavy curls lasted all night (my hair used to be straight by nights end, but now the curls stay in all night without looking over curly). This spray is amazing and smells great.<br /><br />Texture Balm: I have never been able to use texture balm before. It always made my hair look and feel greasy. I love the textured look, but I alsways ended up looking terrible. This is the 1st balm I can use. I rub a bit on my palm and smooth it on my ends. I section my hair by layers to add textured layers. I even tried rubbing my palms over the ends of my hair when it is still damp and after blowdrying I ended up with a straigh style with straigh textured layers. It kept the ends smooth and swingy. I have been doing this more and more.<br /><br />Auto Purchase: I was afraid to do the autobuy. I have heard so many nightmare stories. Here is the truth about the autobuy. You can try a 1 month supply of WEN cleanser and additional extras for a great price like 19.99 or 29.99. These offers usually sign you up for autodelivery automatically. If you dont want auto delivery, you will need to call as soon as you receive the product and cancel. However, I loved the product so much I kept it. Then in 3 weeks they ship you a 3 month supply of WEN & extras + a free product. This is usally about $90. Since it is technically a 3 month supply, they divide the billing by 3 months so you will pay about $30/month. You can manage your account online and change the ship dates. So if my 90 day supply is lasting me more like 120 days, I can push back my next shipment from 3 months to 4 months. You can even change it to 6 months or more, so you will never be inundated. In my experience, if you research the deal there wont be any surprises. If you receive a kit you dont want, or cancel after it has been shipped, you can send it back for a full refund. Also, there will be a letter with a breakdonw of charges and the date each charge will hit in a letter on your box. Make sure to read it so you there are no surprises. If there are, you have the option to return.<br /><br />I dont work for WEN, Ijust love there products! I used shampoo 1 time after using WEN for a month and my hair felt like straw compared to what I was used to. At that very moment I realized I couldnt live without WEN ever again. I never want to go back to the way my hair was. I make sure I always have 1 extra bottle so I never have to use shampoo again. I have now been using WEN for about 6 months.

  412. This is a long review, so here's the short version: Wen makes my hair soft, but that's about it. If only it cost 1/6 of the price, I'd re-buy it. Here's how I determined that: I have long (past shoulders, not yet to mid-back) curly hair that loves humidity (not!), and have been struggling to find a decent product to moisturize my hair and leave it manageable in the summer time. I heard about Wen and decided \\"Well, it'll cost more than I want, but if it works, I can splurge on it regularly\\". I bought the 16 oz bottle thinking it would give me a good introduction to the product without committing myself financially. I watched the \\"How-to\\" videos on the Wen company website - rinsing hair for a few minutes before pumping liberal amounts of the product and working (yes, I brought a comb into the shower, too) through the four sections of your head, adding a splash of water, then letting it sit for at least a few minutes before washing it out. Thus, I was rather psyched up to give the product a try. It has a pleasant smell, but it took me a few showers to get used to the foamy (rather than lather-y) texture of the product. Because I wanted to know the effect the product had on my hair, I cleansed and let my hair air-dry (without any normal styling, blow-drying, etc.). The first day my hair seemed a little frizzy in the morning after the shower, then as the day went on it got less frizzy and more greasy, until the evening when it looked like I needed another shower. But I've heard this is typical, so I didn't worry. I continued to use the product in this manner every day for a week. As the week wore on, my hair had less frizz-to-grease range and balanced out a little more. In addition, I noticed that my hair felt softer than it had with my previous shampoo (Aveeno Active Naturals shampoo + conditioners). I began to use the product every other day after the first week, and added in an anti-frizz serum after the shower, but no further improvementsto the quality (shine, softness, manageability) were noted. With the addition of the anti-frizz product after the shower, my hair behaved as normally as it had using other shampoo/conditioners, though it was softer than using some brands of shampoo/conditioner. Towards the end of the first week and after, I was using about 5 pumps of the product per 1/4 section of my head (meaning 20 pumps to cover my head per shower) and letting it sit on my head for about 10 minutes before rinsing it out. While this is less than recommended, I noticed that while \\"working\\" the product into my hair (and certainly with combing it through) that much of the product ended up on the bottom of my tub and not on my hair. I thus used less product (attempting to extend the lifetime of the bottle) and worked it through more carefully. After the 14-day mark (the equivalent of 10 showers), I was unable to pump more product out of the bottle. Because it has the consistency of a thick conditioner (and because the pump design isn't the best for thick conditioners), some of the product was resting on the inner walls of the bottle and away from the pump's reach. This occurred when there was about 1/4 of the product left (about 4 oz). Since I was determined to get my money's worth out of the bottle, I removed the pump and began trying to shake out approximately 20 pumps for my shower. Not easy to do, but I was able to continue to use the product for another couple showers (picture me, sitting on the floor of my shower, frantically trying to squeeze out every last bit of the Wen product like a frantic drug addict trying to grab at the last scraps of her stash). Not pretty, either. In the end, yes, the product made my hair softer than some other shampoos (namely, Aveeno Active Naturals). But as far as taming frizz or adding manageability or body to my hair, I saw no improvement. So, for the price of a bottle of Wen cleansing conditioner every 2.5 weeks, I determined this product is NOT A WORTHY PRODUCT and NOT A REPEAT BUY.
